Don't waste your Saturday
Take out your MRT card!

A big "Happy 20th Birthday" to the Taipei METRO!

A big Thank You to Taipei Metro and my manager David. The images coming out of Kathmandu are heart breaking. However, this morning I just found out that 7-11 is fundraising to help aid the people of Nepal. Everybody donate what you can. 

When I was in high school I had the chance to visit Nepal for a week, trekking around Annapurna and sightseeing. Nepal is one of the most beautiful countries I've ever been to. It is also one of the poorest. Waking up today, I had two feelings. One was feeling grateful for everything that I have, and the other is wanting to help in any way I can those that don't have very much. ï¼ƒtbt Queens, New York. At first glance, this picture looks like a waste of digital space. There's no subject, nothing of particular interest. But seeing it, I quickly remembered why I took this picture in the first place. In 2006, I went to New York for 5 weeks take part in a play "Mother Courage" at Shakespeare in the Park. While working at Starbucks in Time Square during the day, I relied on the kindness of all my college friends and crashed on countless couches at night. This is what brought me to Queens.

Compared to Manhattan, Queens can seem like the Twilight Zone. It's residential, it's more quiet, there's places to park your car. What this picture doesn't capture, is how incredibly diverse it is. Round the block, there's this Tex-Mex place that I used to go to. I remember walking in, ready to bust out some Spanish when I find out that the owner behind the counter is Chinese. One time I decided to go across the street to the Chinese restaurant for some take out. This time I figure I'll use Mandarin to order my meal only to hear the owner call over his wife in Spanish. Gotta love Queens. A place where one can find intrigue in the most ordinary thing., ä¾†éŒ„å§ï¼

#tbt This is my brother's dog, Sweet Pea. When I moved from Chicago to Los Angeles in 2008 is when I first got to know her. Truth be told, up until then, I didn't like dogs. I thought they were dirty, I thought they smelled. I couldn't understand why anyone would want to have one, or any pet for that matter. It might have something to do with being a paperboy as a kid, and being chased a lot by the neighbor's dog. In any case, ten year old me was terrified of them and I carried my dislike of animals into adulthood. 

Sweet Pea didn't warm up to me right away, either. But on the second day, she came into my room and sat next to my bed and just chilled there. From that point, I decided we'd be great friends. 

I really do believe that Sweet Pea is the best dog in the world. I know, I know, that's what every person says about his or her dog, but Sweet Pea is not my dog. My brother is the one who rescued her and trained her, not me. But I've come to realize that Sweet Pea, and many dogs in general have the ability to embody the best qualities of people. So in such a crummy world, when we watch the news and see people doing destructive things to each other, it's comforting to then take a look at Sweet Pea and be reminded that people can be kind as well. 

One day I noticed that when Sweet Pea sleeps, she curls her entire body up into a ball, and looks very much like a deer. That day, I gave her another name, "Lulu". (Deer Deer, in Mandarin). Whether you say Sweet Pea, or Lulu, she will respond to it. But even that doesn't matter. In my mind, she's just the world's best dog., æ„Ÿå†’å¿«å®Œäº†ï¼Œä»Šå¤©è²éŸ³å¥½ä½ï¼Œå–‰åš¨éƒ½æ˜¯ç—°ã€‚è¶•å¿«ä¾†å–è±†æ¼¿ã€‚Soy milk, perfect remedy for getting rid of a cold. #ç²¥ä¹Ÿä¸éŒ¯, å¥½ä¹…æ²’æœ‰æ–°çš„å½±ç‰‡ï¼ŒçœŸæŠ±æ­‰ï¼ã€Œé›²éœ„é£›è»Šã€MVå¾ˆå¿«å°±æ›å…‰äº†ï¼æˆ‘ä¸Šæ˜ŸæœŸåœ¨å°åŒ—å…’ç«¥æ–°æ¨‚åœ’æ‹é å‘Šï¼ä¸–ç•Œä¸Šæœ€åˆºæ¿€çš„é›²éœ„é£›è»Šåœ¨å“ªè£¡ï¼ŸWhere's the world's craziest roller coaster ride? Elbo Room, Chicago, June 22, 2008

That's me on stage introducing myself to the crowd, on a sweaty summer night. To my right is P, singing backup, with Bev on drums, and Ritch on guitar. 

The bar was across from the stage, where about forty people crammed into a small space, drinking the night away. Hot, noisy, your typical local music venue. Just because people were talking loudly through your set, didn't necessarily mean they weren't listening to the music. 

I always think of these performances as my great indie music education. If you could sing a song from beginning to end at the corner dive, then surely, you could sing anywhere., ç‡ˆç‡ˆï¼

#tbt          Shakespeare's "The Tempest" - Act I Sc. 2b, Shanley Pavilion, 2004. 

        While I often talk about music and singing, I rarely mention my love of the theater. In college, good opportunities to perform on stage were hard to come by. For the longest time I blamed this on racial discrimination. I thought everybody was prejudiced and unable to see my Asian face portraying anything on stage. Even my theater professors had difficulty choosing scripts for me to study. Then in my last year, my classmate Mark decided to cast me in a student production of Shakespeare's "The Tempest" as the lead role, Prospero, duke of Milan.

         Jessica, the girl on the left, plays my daughter, can you believe it? Thinking back, I'm thankful that Mark was progressive and used multi-racial casting for the show. Never mind the fact that me and my stage daughter, in real life, are only 3 years apart in age. (Hey, it's college and college is awesome like that.)  In a nod to Kurosawa, Mark also re-contextualized the setting to feudal Japan. (Because, why the hell, not, after all?)

          This was my only substantial experience in college, the only time I got to tear into a great role. I cherish it, even now. And then, there's Shakespeare. The language in the play. Before "The Tempest" I was already into the Bard but Prospero made me a die-hard fan., è¬è¬ one FM çš„DJï¼Œè¬è¬å¤§é¦¬çš„åª’é«”ï¼Œæ­Œè¿·ï¼æˆ‘å¾ˆæ¦®å¹¸ä»Šå¤©ç²å¾—åå¤§å°ˆè¼¯ã€å‹çˆ†30æ’è¡Œæ¦œå¹´åº¦ç¸½é¸2014å…¨å®‡å®™æœ€æ„›æ–°äººï¼æˆ‘ä¸€å®šè¦å¾ˆå¿«å†å›ä¾†å¤§é¦¬è¡¨æ¼”ï¼

Ahhhh! Thank you, One FM, Malaysian media, and all my awesome fans!! So honored to be voted 'Fan Choice #1 New Artist' at the one FM annual Awards 2014. Can't wait to come back soon with new music!

#tbt Good Friday, 2008, Chicago. This picture was taken on an actual digital camera in my pre-smartphone owning days. Standing in the doorway of my old apartment I see Europa bookstore and Johnny's Grill further up. Out of view behind me is the Starbucks where I used to work. It was convenient to say the least, living right above it. I lived here in this little spot for 3 years before moving to LA. This must be the last time I saw snow., ç‚ºä»€éº¼æ”¾ç©ºäº†å¹¾ç§’ï¼Ÿ

It's Thanksgiving today in America. Although we don't really celebrate it here in Taiwan, I still want to express my gratitude. So much to be thankful for this year: I made my professional debut, traveled the world, and met so many wonderful fans who support and encourage the music. It's no wonder I want to put my hands together and thank my Creator for all these blessings. 

World events in the newspapers have seemed especially bleak these past few days. It gives me perspective seeing the challenges that every nation faces. I can only hope that we as people, learn to peacefully overcome each obstacle. Sometimes it feels as if we've all forgotten how to forgive one another.  Incidentally, a friend recently taught me a new saying: "water under the bridge". On a day such as this, this phrase seems particularly appropriate. Let bygones be bygones, forgive one another, and together walk step by step into the future. 

Didn't mean to rant this long. I just want to say one thing, really: Thank you all. Let's all fight this together., è² è² å¾—æ­£, thank you, Singaporean fans for the hat!

Just watched 'The Maze Runner' and really enjoyed it. It wasn't the script (honestly, Hunger Games has a better story line) and it wasn't the special effects. Rather, it was because one of the supporting roles was Asian American and he rocked. In Hollywood, you rarely see a decent Asian American role that doesn't rely on stereotypes. Opportunities for Asian American actors are so few and when we do get them, they cause for many of us, an existential crisis. But tonight's movie had none of the usual fare. When I was growing up I wanted to be on Broadway. My mom would take me to the theater and I dreamed of being just like the actors on stage, performing in front of a live audience. In college I even studied opera and musical theater. Upon graduation, however, I realized that I enjoyed songwriting even more and so my aspirations for Broadway were left behind. 

Watching yesterday's opening performance of "The Phantom of the Opera" brought me back to that time studying opera. I remembered aspiring to be like each of the performers yesterday, who were all excellent. (The Phantom score may be pop, but it is certainly difficult). 

This morning I woke up in the mood to sing some opera. Who wants to sing some opera with me?! Jess Lee, I know you're a coloratura. And I have a book of arias and duets lying around somewhere., æ­ŒåŠ‡é­…å½± é¦–æ¼”ä¹‹å¤œ At "The Phantom of Opera, opening night, Taipei æ¢æ–‡éŸ³ æåƒå¨œ, å¤§å®¶æ™šå®‰ï¼ä¸è¦åƒå¤ªå¤šï¼å“ˆå“ˆã€‚Goodnight everyone! Chinese herbs. Woke up with a hoarse throat so my mom suggests I buy some Chinese herbs. Because I haven't a clue when it comes to finding a Chinese pharmacy, I asked the boss of my favorite noodle shop if she knew where I could buy said herbs. Not only did she know, but she stopped what she was doing and walked me to the nearest pharmacy. I was at once embarrassed for taking time away from her job and moved by the thoughtfulness. Feeling better already., Hace calor

Why I love Taipei:

Me getting into a cab:

"I'm so angry! The line at the ticket booth for the train was so long that I missed my train! Annoyed as hell!"

Cab driver: 

"Don't be angry, man. C'mon, how about a beer? I'll have one with you. That way you won't be so angry when you get to where you're going."

Anger: 0

Taipei: 1, THUNDER!!
